if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Metric_(band)';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"band,metric,(,_,),";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Metric</b>
is
a
<a
href="/wiki/Canadian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Canadian"
class="mw-redirect">Canadian</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
founded
in
1998
in
<a
href="/wiki/Toronto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
have
also
at
various
times
been
based
in
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London">London</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
consists
of
<a
href="/wiki/Emily_Haines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emily
Haines">Emily
Haines</a>
(lead
vocals,
<a
href="/wiki/Synthesizers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthesizers"
class="mw-redirect">synthesizers</a>,
guitar,
tambourine,
harmonica,
piano),
<a
href="/wiki/James_Shaw_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Shaw
(musician)">James
Shaw</a>
(guitar,
synthesizers,
<a
href="/wiki/Theremin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Theremin">theremin</a>,
backing
vocals),
<a
href="/wiki/Joshua_Winstead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joshua
Winstead">Joshua
Winstead</a>
(bass,
synthesizers,
backing
vocals)
and
Joules
Scott-Key
(drums,
percussion).</p>








<p>The
band
started
in
1998
as
a
duo
formed
by
Haines
and
Shaw.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Initially,
the
duo's
name
was
Mainstream.<sup
id="cite_ref-spinmag_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spinmag-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
releasing
an
EP
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
EP">Mainstream
EP</a></i>,
they
changed
the
band's
name
to
Metric,
after
a
sound
that
was
programmed
by
Shaw
on
his
keyboard
in
1998.<sup
id="cite_ref-spinmag_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spinmag-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001,
Winstead
and
Scott-Key
joined
them.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Haines
and
Shaw
also
perform
with
the

and

moniker,
she
released
in
2006
the
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Knives_Don%27t_Have_Your_Back?qsrc=3044"

and

released

one
live
DVD:
<i>Live
at
Metropolis</i>
(2008);
plus
a
string
of
singles.</p>








<p>Their
first
official
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Old_World_Underground,_Where_Are_You_Now%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?">Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</a></i>,
was
released
in
September
2,
2003.
It
was
followed
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_It_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
It
Out">Live
It
Out</a></i>,
released
on
October
4,
2005.
The
album
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/2006_Polaris_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2006
Polaris
Music
Prize">2006
Polaris
Music
Prize</a>
for
the
&quot;Canadian
Album
of
the
Year&quot;
and
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Juno_Awards_of_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juno
Awards
of
2006">2006
Juno
Awards</a>
for
&quot;Best
Alternative
Album&quot;.</p>








<p>Their
third
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a></i>
was
recorded
in
2001
and
it
was
initially
planned
as
their
debut
album.
The
album
was
delayed
for
many
years
and
it
was
finally
released
in
June
26,
2007,
with
some
changes
in
track
list.
Some
songs
were
also
slightly
reworked.</p>








<p>Metric's
fourth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fantasies_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fantasies
(album)">Fantasies</a></i>
was
released
in
April
7,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
shortlisted
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/2009_Polaris_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2009
Polaris
Music
Prize">2009
Polaris
Music
Prize</a>
for
&quot;Canadian
Album
of
the
Year&quot;,
and
won
the
&quot;Alternative
Album
of
the
Year&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Juno_Awards_of_2010?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juno
Awards
of
2010">2010
Juno
Awards</a>.
Metric
won
as
well
in
2010
&quot;Group
of
the
Year&quot;.
<i>Fantasies</i>
also
became
the
band's
most
successful
album
so
far.</p>








<p>The
fifth
Metric
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Synthetica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthetica">Synthetica</a></i>,
was
released
on
June
12,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
won
two
awards
at
<a
href="/wiki/Juno_Awards_of_2013?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juno
Awards
of
2013">2013
Juno
Awards</a>:
&quot;Alternative
Album
of
the
Year&quot;
for
<i>Synthetica</i>
and
&quot;Producer
of
the
Year&quot;
for
James
Shaw.
The
art
director/designer/photographer
Justin
Broadbent
also
won
an
award
for
&quot;Recording
Package
of
the
Year&quot;
for
<i>Synthetica</i>.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_early_years">Formation
and
early
years</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
early
years">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Born
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_Delhi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Delhi">New
Delhi</a>,
India,
and
raised
in
<a
href="/wiki/Cache_Bay,_Ontario?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cache
Bay,
Ontario"
class="mw-redirect">Cache
Bay</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Ontario?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ontario">Ontario</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Emily_Haines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emily
Haines">Emily
Haines</a>
grew
up
as
a
dual
citizen
of
both
Canada
and
the
United
States,
the
latter
due
to
her
American-born
parents.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
daughter
of
poet
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Haines_(poet)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Haines
(poet)">Paul
Haines</a>
(best
known
for
his
lyrical
collaboration
with
<a
href="/wiki/Carla_Bley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carla
Bley">Carla
Bley</a>
in
the
1971
jazz
opera
<i><a
href="/wiki/Escalator_over_the_Hill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Escalator
over
the
Hill">Escalator
over
the
Hill</a></i>),
Haines
left
London
at
the
age
of
three.
Paul
would
often
make
cassettes
of
rare
and
eclectic
music
for
his
daughter
to
listen
to,
and
her
early
influences
included
Carla
Bley
and
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Wyatt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Wyatt">Robert
Wyatt</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Haines
attended
<a
href="/wiki/Etobicoke_School_of_the_Arts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Etobicoke
School
of
the
Arts">Etobicoke
School
of
the
Arts</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
There
she
met
<a
href="/wiki/Amy_Millan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amy
Millan">Amy
Millan</a>
(future
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/Stars_(Canadian_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stars
(Canadian
band)">Stars</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Broken_Social_Scene?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Broken
Social
Scene">Broken
Social
Scene</a>),
and
<a
href="/wiki/Kevin_Drew?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kevin
Drew">Kevin
Drew</a>
(future
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/Broken_Social_Scene?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Broken
Social
Scene">Broken
Social
Scene</a>).<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_1-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Haines
and
Millan
briefly
formed
their
first
band
around
1990
while
at
ESA.
Haines
attended
the
University
of
British
Columbia
in
<a
href="/wiki/Vancouver?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>
in
1992–1993,
at
<a
href="/wiki/Toronto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toronto">Toronto</a>
in
1995,
and
at
<a
href="/wiki/Concordia_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concordia
University">Concordia
University</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>
in
1995–1996.
She
distributed
in
1996
an
early
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cut_in_Half_and_Also_Double?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cut
in
Half
and
Also
Double">Cut
in
Half
and
Also
Double</a></i>
with
a
limited
number
of
copies,
that
included
songs
written
and
recorded
during
her
student
years.</p>








<p>UK
born
<a
href="/wiki/James_Shaw_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Shaw
(musician)">James
Shaw</a>
was
a
student
at
a
<a
href="/wiki/Boston?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston">Boston</a>
music
school
and
was
friends
with
<a
href="/wiki/Torquil_Campbell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Torquil
Campbell">Torquil
Campbell</a>,
a
vocalist
who
would
later
form
<a
href="/wiki/Stars_(Canadian_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stars
(Canadian
band)">Stars</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Seligman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Seligman"
class="mw-redirect">Chris
Seligman</a>,
the
future
synthesizer
player
of
Stars.
Torquil
had
plans
to
move
to
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>
and
on
his
suggestion,
Shaw
applied
to
<a
href="/wiki/Juilliard_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juilliard
School">Juilliard
Music
School</a>
and
moved
to
New
York
with
him.
After
a
three-year
education
at
the
institution,
Shaw
had
acquired
considerable
classical
training
but
did
not
enjoy
his
stay
and
knew
his
musical
interests
lay
elsewhere.
Shaw
and
Torquil
returned
to
<a
href="/wiki/Toronto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.</p>








<p>Emily
Haines
met
<a
href="/wiki/James_Shaw_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Shaw
(musician)">James
Shaw</a>
in
Toronto
in
1997.
The
two
of
them
began
dating
and
writing
songs
together.
In
the
same
year,
Shaw
released
his
studio
album,
<i>Life
on
the
Clock</i>,
which
also
featured
Haines
singing
on
some
songs.
Shaw
also
moved
to
Montreal
where
Haines
was
still
living.
In
1998,
they
self-released
an
EP
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
EP">Mainstream
EP</a></i>,
that
contained
5
tracks
with
an
overall
<a
href="/wiki/Downtempo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Downtempo">downtempo</a>
and
electronic
feel.
Haines
later
revealed
that
the
band
was
called
Mainstream
at
the
time:
&quot;the
very
first
name
that
Jimmy
and
I
had
was
Mainstream.
We
put
out
an
EP
under
that
name&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-spinmag_2-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spinmag-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Metric_live_2005.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Metric_live_2005.jpg/220px-Metric_live_2005.jpg"

class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Metric_live_2005.jpg/330px-Metric_live_2005.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Metric_live_2005.jpg/440px-Metric_live_2005.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Metric_live_2005.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Metric
live
2005









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>A
bit
later
they
changed
the
name
to
Metric.<sup
id="cite_ref-spinmag_2-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spinmag-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
<a
href="/wiki/Emily_Haines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emily
Haines">Emily
Haines</a>,
the
name
&quot;came
from
a
song
that
Jimmy
[Shaw]
and
I
were
working
on
back
in
Toronto
in
the
early
days,
like
'97
or
'98.
Jimmy
had
a
song
that
involved
a
sound
he'd
programmed
into
his
keyboard
and
called
'Metric'.
When
we
saw
that
word
on
the
keyboard's
LED
screen
it
looked
so
electro.
It
had
a
no
bullshit
vibe.
It
was
a
little
cold
and
standoffish
and
we're
down
with
that.
It
works
for
us.
Some
people
think
it
has
something
to
do
with
the
fact
that
we're
from
Canada
--
which
uses
the
metric
system.
That
was
coincidental,
though
at
the
time
we
were
into
arty
electronic
stuff
that
was
coming
out
of
European
countries
that
also
use
the
metric
system.
But
if
we'd
wanted
to
use
a
name
that
evoked
Canada,
we
would've
called
ourselves
the
Toques
or
something&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-spinmag_2-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-spinmag-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
fall
of
1998,
Shaw
moved
back
to
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>,
this
time
accompanied
by
Haines,
Campbell,
and
Seligman.
There
they
shared
a
<a
href="/wiki/Loft?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loft">loft</a>
in
the
Williamsburg
section
of
<a
href="/wiki/Brooklyn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>.
During
their
two-year
stay
at
the
loft,
Haines
and
Shaw
were
erstwhile
roommates
with
future
members
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Yeah_Yeah_Yeahs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yeah
Yeah
Yeahs">Yeah
Yeah
Yeahs</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Liars_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liars
(band)">Liars</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/TV_on_the_Radio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="TV
on
the
Radio">TV
on
the
Radio</a>.
In
an
interview
with
91X
FM
radio,
Shaw
said
that
although
this
sounded
like
an
amazing
place
to
live,
they
were
broke
and
&quot;it
was
difficult
for
everyone
involved&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>That
same
year,
<a
href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warner
Bros.
Records">Warner
Bros.
Records</a>
showed
interest
in
the
group
and
the
band
did
a
development
deal
with
them.
A
producer
in
<a
href="/wiki/London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="London">London</a>
saw
the
potential
of
commercial
success
from
the
demos
they
recorded
in
this
period
and
offered
to
bring
Metric
to
the
UK
for
a
possible
record
deal.
Eager
to
take
a
break
from
the
somewhat
miserable
conditions
of
the
loft,
Haines
and
Shaw
set
off
to
London
in
early
2000
and
signed
a
publishing
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Chrysalis_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chrysalis
Records">Chrysalis
Records</a>.</p>








<p>With
the
help
of
the
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Hague?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stephen
Hague">Stephen
Hague</a>
(who
had
produced
acts
like
<a
href="/wiki/Erasure?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Erasure">Erasure</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/New_Order?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Order">New
Order</a>,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pet_Shop_Boys?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pet
Shop
Boys">Pet
Shop
Boys</a>),
Metric
worked
on
a
new
batch
of
<a
href="/wiki/New_wave_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
wave
music">new
wave</a>/<a
href="/wiki/Synthpop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthpop">synthpop</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Drum_machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drum
machine">drum
machine</a>
paced
songs.
Although
Metric
already
had
a
semi-mainstream
appeal,
they
felt
restricted
by
the
confines
of
recording
demos
and
were
eager
to
return
to
NYC
and
put
a
live
band
together.
In
November
2000,
they
moved
back
to
their
Brooklyn
loft.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away_.282001.E2.80.932002.29"><i>Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</i>
(2001–2002)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away
(2001–2002)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a>







</div>








<p>Metric
continued
to
work
on
their
debut
album
in
the
first
few
months
of
2001.
Now
dubbed
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a></i>,
the
effort
revealed
a
more
musically
layered
and
mature
sound
than
the
earlier
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_EP?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
EP">Mainstream
EP</a></i>.
Haines
and
Shaw
completed
the
album
in
April
and
by
this
time
had
found
a
new
label
for
their
release,
the
L.A.
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_record_label?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
record
label">indie
label</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Restless_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Restless
Records">Restless
Records</a>.
The
album
(produced
by
Shaw)
was
delayed
for
years
by
their
record
label,
Restless
Records.
It
will
be
finally
released
in
2007
on
<a
href="/wiki/Last_Gang_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Gang
Records">Last
Gang
Records</a>.</p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a></i>
included
<a
href="/wiki/Uptempo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Uptempo"
class="mw-redirect">uptempo</a>
songs
such
as
the
title
track
&quot;Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away&quot;,
&quot;Raw
Sugar&quot;,
and
&quot;Soft
Rock
Star&quot;,
<a
href="/wiki/Downtempo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Downtempo">downtempo</a>
songs
like
&quot;White
Gold&quot;,
&quot;The
Twist&quot;,
and
&quot;Rock
Me
Now&quot;
(which
included
singing
by
Shaw,
spoken-word
vocals
by
Haines
in
a
manner
reminiscent
of
&quot;The
Mandate&quot;,
and
had
an
overall
jazzy
vibe).
&quot;Parkdale&quot;,
featuring
trumpeting
by
Shaw
and
a
fanfare
intro,
concerned
the
<a
href="/wiki/Parkdale,_Toronto?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parkdale,
Toronto">Parkdale,
Toronto</a>
neighborhood.
When
the
track
titled
&quot;Rock
Me
Now&quot;
was
reworked,
it
had
been
stripped
of
its
intro
&quot;bubble&quot;
sounds,
as
well
as
an
additional
vocal
part
was
added
to
the
bridge.
The
title
track
was
also
reworked
during
the
chorus,
in
which,
Haines
vocalizes
&quot;
If
this
is
the
life,
why
does
it
feel
so
good
to
die
today?&quot;
and
the
synths
get
a
more
&quot;heavier&quot;
feel.</p>








<p>In
the
same
year,
the
band
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Static_Anonymity?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Static
Anonymity">Static
Anonymity</a></i>,
an
EP
which
consisted
of
5
songs.
Three
tracks
from
the
EP
also
featured
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a></i>.
The
EP
was
only
available
at
Metric
performances
and
on
their
official
site.
The
EP
comes
with
a
very
limited
track
listing
(as
aforementioned
it
had
only
consisted
of
five
whole
tracks)
Track
listing
(natural
order)
1.
Grow
up
and
blow
away
2.
Siamese
cities
3.
Down
4.
Soft
rock
star
(
jimmy
versus
joe
remix)
5.
London
halflife</p>

class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=Metric_live_at_the_9-30_Club,_2004.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:Metric
live
at

9-30

live
at
the
9-30

2004.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










Metric
live
at
the
9:30
Club,
2004









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
the
winter
of
2001,
Metric
had
gained
two
new
bandmates:
the
<a
href="/wiki/Drummer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drummer">drummer</a>
Joules
Scott-Key
(a
native
of
Flint,
Michigan)
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bassist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bassist">bassist</a>
Joshua
Winstead
(a
native
from
Texas).
Scott-Key
attended
college
in
Texas
and
was
in
town
with
his
friend
Winstead
performing
in
the
local
music
scene.
Scott-Key
(no
relation
to
<a
href="/wiki/Francis_Scott_Key?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Francis
Scott
Key">Francis
Scott
Key</a>)
and
Winstead
had
known
each
other
for
about
a
decade
and
they
met
Haines
and
Shaw
at
the
Brooklyn
loft
and
at
local
performances.</p>








<p>Metric
at
the
time
was
for
the
most
part
a
studio
band
and
live
shows
approximated
the
<a
href="/wiki/Synthesizer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthesizer">synthesizer</a>-centered
and
<a
href="/wiki/Drum_machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drum
machine">drum
machine</a>-driven
sound
of
the
recordings.
The
recruitment
of
a
drummer
and
a
bassist,
facilitated
a
stronger,
more
engaging
live
presence.
Metric
performed
in
New
York
in
early
spring
and
late
summer
2001,
personally
circulating
handmade
CD-R
copies
of
their
unreleased
music
to
fans
at
shows
and
by
mail,
eventually
giving
the
music
away
for
free
on
the
internet.</p>








<p>Metric
received
their
first
major
public
exposure
in
August
2001
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Television_commercial?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Television
commercial"
class="mw-redirect">television
commercial</a>
&quot;Be
Afraid&quot;,
advertising
<a
href="/wiki/Polaroid_Corporation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Polaroid
Corporation">Polaroid</a>'s
I-Zone
Pocket
Fortune
film.
The
music
used
for
the
ad
was
taken
from
the
song
&quot;Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away&quot;,
with
the
line
&quot;Why
does
it
feel
so
good
to
die
today?&quot;
changed
to
&quot;Why
does
it
feel
so
good
to
fly
away?&quot;.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Old_World_Underground.2C_Where_Are_You_Now.3F_.282003.E2.80.932004.29"><i>Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</i>
(2003–2004)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?
(2003–2004)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Old_World_Underground,_Where_Are_You_Now%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?">Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</a>







</div>








<p>In
2003,
Metric
released
their
first
official
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Old_World_Underground,_Where_Are_You_Now%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?">Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</a></i>
on
<a
href="/wiki/Last_Gang_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Gang
Records">Last
Gang
Records</a>.
The
album
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Andrews_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Andrews
(musician)">Michael
Andrews</a>
and
it
was
recorded
at
Elgonix
Labs,
Los
Angeles,
USA.
<i>Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</i>
received
generally
positive
reviews.
As
of
12
December
2005,
the
album
has
gone
<a
href="/wiki/Gold_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gold
record"
class="mw-redirect">gold</a>
in
Canada.</p>








<p>The
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Combat_Baby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Combat
Baby"
class="mw-redirect">Combat
Baby</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Dead
Disco&quot;
were
released
as
singles.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Combat_Baby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Combat
Baby"
class="mw-redirect">Combat
Baby</a>&quot;
was
featured
as
a
free
single
on
iTunes
in
2004.
Also
there
were
made
six
music
videos
for
the
following
songs:
&quot;Calculation
Theme&quot;,
&quot;IOU&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Combat_Baby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Combat
Baby"
class="mw-redirect">Combat
Baby</a>&quot;,
&quot;Succexy&quot;,
&quot;The
List&quot;,
&quot;Dead
Disco&quot;.</p>








<p>Metric
was
featured
as
themselves
in
the
2004
independent
French
film,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Clean_(2004_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clean
(2004
film)"
class="mw-redirect">Clean</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Olivier_Assayas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Olivier
Assayas">Olivier
Assayas</a>
and
starring
<a
href="/wiki/Maggie_Cheung?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Maggie
Cheung">Maggie
Cheung</a>.
The
band
performed
the
song
&quot;Dead
Disco&quot;
in
the
film
and
also
acted
in
a
short
sequence.
The
film
was
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Palme_D%27Or?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Palme
D'Or"
class="mw-redirect">Palme
D'Or</a>
award
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cannes
Film
Festival">Cannes
Film
Festival</a>.
The
soundtrack
also
features
songs
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brian_Eno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brian
Eno">Brian
Eno</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Daniel_Lanois?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Daniel
Lanois">Daniel
Lanois</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Emily_Haines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emily
Haines">Emily
Haines</a>,
Metric
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tricky_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tricky
(musician)">Tricky</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Live_It_Out_and_Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away_.282005.E2.80.932007.29"><i>Live
It
Out</i>
and
<i>Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</i>
(2005–2007)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
Live
It
Out
and
Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away
(2005–2007)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
articles:









<a
href="/wiki/Live_It_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
It
Out">Live
It
Out</a>
and









<a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a>







</div>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:132px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=Metric_live_at_Washington,_DC_2006.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:Metric
live
at
Washington,
DC
2006.jpg">File:Metric

at

2006.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










Metric
live
at
Washington,
DC
2006









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>On
October
4,
2005,
Metric
released
their
second
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_It_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
It
Out">Live
It
Out</a></i>,
on
<a
href="/wiki/Last_Gang_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Gang
Records">Last
Gang
Records</a>.
The
album,
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/James_Shaw_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Shaw
(musician)">James
Shaw</a>,
was
well
received
by
critics
and
fans.
<i>Live
It
Out</i>
was
a
success
in
Canada,
already
selling
twice
as
many
copies
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Old_World_Underground,_Where_Are_You_Now%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?">Old
World
Underground,
Where
Are
You
Now?</a></i>.
The
album
has
since
gone
twice
<a
href="/wiki/Platinum_record?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Platinum
record"
class="mw-redirect">platinum</a>
in
Canada,
selling
over
200,000
units.</p>








<p>Three
singles
supported
the
album'
sales:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monster_Hospital?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monster
Hospital">Monster
Hospital</a>&quot;
(number
55
on
<a
href="/wiki/UK_singles_charts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
singles
charts"
class="mw-redirect">UK
singles
charts</a>),
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Poster_of_a_Girl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Poster
of
a
Girl"
class="mw-redirect">Poster
of
a
Girl</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Empty_(Metric_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Empty
(Metric
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Empty</a>&quot;.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monster_Hospital?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monster
Hospital">Monster
Hospital</a>&quot;
was
selected
as
<a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a>
Track
of
the
Week<sup
id="cite_ref-nme_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nme-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
also
featured
at
number
12
on
NME
Tracks
of
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-nme_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nme-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Live
It
Out</i>
also
featured
at
number
38
at
NME
Recordings
of
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-nme_8-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nme-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
this
time,
Metric
was
approached
by
and
agreed
to
open
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stones"
class="mw-redirect">Rolling
Stones</a>
whose
tour
coincided
with
theirs
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
York
City">New
York
City</a>.
The
band
did
a
UK-wide
tour
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/Bloc_Party?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bloc
Party">Bloc
Party</a>
as
well
as
performing
at
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_and_Leeds_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
and
Leeds
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
and
Leeds
Festival</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Great_Escape_(festival)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Great
Escape
(festival)">The
Great
Escape</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Brighton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brighton">Brighton</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Wireless_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wireless
Festival">Wireless
Festival</a>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hyde
Park,
London">Hyde
Park</a>
in
London
and
numerous
club
dates
throughout
the
UK.
The
band
has
toured
the
world
extensively
for
several
years
playing
concerts
in
France,
Germany,
Iceland,
Brazil,
Greece,
Italy,
Turkey,
the
Netherlands,
Finland,
Belgium,
Sweden,
Norway,
United
States,
Canada,
Venezuela,
Mexico
and
Japan
to
promote
<i>Live
it
Out</i>.</p>








<p>On
June
26,
2007,
<a
href="/wiki/Last_Gang_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Last
Gang
Records">Last
Gang
Records</a>
released
Metric's
2001
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grow_Up_and_Blow_Away?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away">Grow
Up
and
Blow
Away</a></i>,
with
an
altered
track
listing
compared
to
the
unofficial
version.
There
were
added
the
songs
&quot;London
Halflife&quot;
and
&quot;Soft
Rock
Star&quot;
(Jimmy
vs.
Joe
mix)
from
the
2001
EP
<i><a
href="/wiki/Static_Anonymity?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Static
Anonymity">Static
Anonymity</a></i>
and
removed
the
songs
&quot;Torture
Me&quot;,
&quot;Fanfare&quot;
and
&quot;Parkdale&quot;.
Also
the
order
of
some
songs
was
changed
and
some
songs
(like
the
title
track
and
&quot;Rock
Me
Now&quot;)
were
slightly
reworked.</p>








<p>Throughout
the
summer
of
2007,
four
new
songs
were
road-tested
by
the
band,
tentatively
named
&quot;Black
Sheep&quot;,
&quot;The
Hooks&quot;,
&quot;Stadium
Love&quot;,
and
&quot;Up
in
Flames&quot;.
On
October
4,
2007,
Metric
played
a
live
webcast
show
on
<a
href="/wiki/Myspace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Myspace">Myspace</a>'s
&quot;Hey
Play
This&quot;
programme.
Fans
sent
in
requests
and
the
band
played
a
selected
few.
Along
with
old
material,
they
performed
several
new
songs,
including
&quot;Freddie&quot;
(aka
&quot;Black
Sheep&quot;),
&quot;Standing
in
Line&quot;,
&quot;Gimme
Sympathy&quot;
(aka
&quot;The
Hooks&quot;),
&quot;Twilight&quot;,
&quot;Joyride&quot;
and
&quot;Stadium
Love&quot;.</p>








<p>On
November
13,
2007,
Last
Gang
Records
released
a
trailer
on
<a
href="/wiki/YouTube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="YouTube">YouTube</a>
for
a
Metric
<a
href="/wiki/DVD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="DVD">DVD</a>
showcasing
a
live
concert
at
the
Metropolis
Theatre
in
<a
href="/wiki/Montreal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreal">Montreal</a>,
as
well
as
all
three
music
videos
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Live_It_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
It
Out">Live
It
Out</a></i>.
The
DVD
titled
<i>Live
at
Metropolis</i>
was
released
on
February
12,
2008.
A
three-track
audio
<a
href="/wiki/Extended_play?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extended
play">EP</a>
was
released
on
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>
in
December.
The
EP
features
the
live
tracks
&quot;The
Police
and
the
Private&quot;,
&quot;Too
Little
Too
Late&quot;
and
&quot;Patriarch
on
a
Vespa&quot;
from
the
DVD,
as
well
as
the
DVD
trailer.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Fantasies_.282008.E2.80.932011.29"><i>Fantasies</i>
(2008–2011)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Fantasies
(2008–2011)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Fantasies_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fantasies
(album)">Fantasies
(album)</a>







</div>








<p>The
band
performed
select
dates
in
2008
in
Canada,
Mexico
and
Brazil
while
continuing
to
record
their
upcoming
fourth
album.
They
performed
at
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella
Festival</a>
on
April
27,
2008,<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
at
the
2008
<a
href="/wiki/Ottawa_Bluesfest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ottawa
Bluesfest">Ottawa
Bluesfest</a>
on
July
11,
2008
in
addition
to
playing
at
the
2008
<a
href="/wiki/Pemberton_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pemberton
Festival">Pemberton
Festival</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Pemberton,_British_Columbia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pemberton,
British
Columbia">Pemberton,
British
Columbia</a>
on
July
25,
2008
and
<a
href="/wiki/All_Points_West_Music_%26_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
Points
West
Music
&amp;
Arts
Festival">All
Points
West
Music
&amp;
Arts
Festival</a>
in
New
Jersey
on
August
9,
2008.</p>








<p>During
December
13–23,
2008,
Metric
toured
across
Canada
with
<a
href="/wiki/Tokyo_Police_Club?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tokyo
Police
Club">Tokyo
Police
Club</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Dears?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Dears">The
Dears</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Sebastien_Grainger_and_The_Mountains?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sebastien
Grainger
and
The
Mountains"
class="mw-redirect">Sebastien
Grainger
and
The
Mountains</a>,
to
raise
money
for
various
charities
under
the
name
&quot;Jingle
Bell
Rock&quot;
tour.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Help,_I%27m_Alive?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Help,
I'm
Alive"
class="mw-redirect">Help,
I'm
Alive</a>&quot;
was
officially
released
as
the
lead
single
from
the
upcoming
album
on
iTunes
on
December
23,
2008
in
Canada
and
January
1,
2009
around
the
rest
of
the
world.</p>








<p>Their
fourth
record,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fantasies_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fantasies
(album)">Fantasies</a></i>,
was
self-released
on
April
7,
2009
through
their
own
label,
Metric
Music
International.
The
album
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Gavin_Brown_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gavin
Brown
(musician)">Gavin
Brown</a>
and
James
Shaw
and
it
was
recorded
at
<a
href="/wiki/Electric_Lady_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electric
Lady
Studios">Electric
Lady
Studios</a>,
New
York.
<i>Fantasies</i>
was
issued
in
multiple
versions:
standard
edition
(featuring
10
tracks),
deluxe
edition
(including
4
more
tracks),
deluxe
edition
UK
edition
(including
10
more
tracks),
and
later,
Expanded
Edition
(a
second
disc
with
10
tracks).</p>








<p><i>Fantasies</i>
was
generally
well
received
by
critics
and
fans.
As
of
2012
it
has
sold
500,000
copies,
becoming
the
band's
best
selling
album
so
far.
All
10
tracks
were
previously
performed
acoustically
by
Haines
and
Shaw
on
September
7,
2008,
at
Union
Pool
in
Brooklyn
under
the
premises
of
an
Emily
Haines
solo
show.</p>

class="thumb
tright">

<p>The
music
video
for
&quot;Gimme
Sympathy&quot;
was
released
on
<a
href="/wiki/Myspace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Myspace">Myspace</a>
on
March
16,
2009.
Emily
and
Jimmy
completed
a
mini
tour
of
exclusive
acoustic
shows
across
Canada,
with
stops
in
Winnipeg,
Edmonton,
Calgary,
Vancouver,
and
Victoria
in
late
April
with
cooperation
from
local
radio
stations.
The
band
finished
a
Europe
tour
in
May
2009
and
toured
the
US
(with
Sebastien
Grainger
and
The
Mountains
and
Smile
Smile),
UK,
and
Canada
at
certain
music
festivals
during
the
summer.
They
then
headed
to
Australia
for
their
first
ever
Australian
tour
in
early
October,
as
well
as
one
show
in
Tokyo.</p>








<p>On
August
30,
2009,
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Shinoda">Mike
Shinoda</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Linkin_Park?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Linkin
Park">Linkin
Park</a>
fame
made
his
remix
of
the
track
&quot;Gold
Guns
Girls&quot;
available
for
streaming
on
his
website.
He
used
the
remix
as
the
theme
for
his
art
exhibition
Glorious
Excess
(Dies),
and
later
became
part
of
a
compilation
album
set
up
by
Linkin
Park's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Music_for_Relief?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
for
Relief">Music
for
Relief</a></i>
for
victims
of
the
2010
Haiti
earthquake.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
October
27,
2009,
Metric
released
a
5-track
EP
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Plug_in_Plug_Out?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Plug
in
Plug
Out">Plug
in
Plug
Out</a></i>
containing
acoustic
versions
of
songs
from
<i>Fantasies</i>.
The
EP
was
available
exclusively
on
<a
href="/wiki/Amazon.com?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a>
for
30
days.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2009,
the
band
produced
a
<a
rel="nofollow"
class="external
text"
href="http://www.yellowbirdproject.com/products/metric">charity
t-shirt</a>
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Yellow_Bird_Project?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yellow
Bird
Project">Yellow
Bird
Project</a>
to
raise
funding
to
promote
musical
education
across
Canada.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
t-shirt
bears
the
slogan
'Keep
the
dream
tight'
-
a
lyric
from
their
song,
&quot;Hustle
Rose&quot;.</p>








<p>Emily
and
Jimmy
performed
an
acoustic
version
of
&quot;Help
I'm
Alive&quot;
on
January
22,
2010
for
the
Canada
for
Haiti
telethon.
During
the
<a
href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2010
Winter
Olympics">2010
Winter
Olympics</a>,
Metric,
along
with
several
other
Canadian
music
acts,
came
together
in
Vancouver
to
re-record
<a
href="/wiki/K%27Naan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="K'Naan"
class="mw-redirect">K'Naan</a>'s
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wavin%27_Flag?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wavin'
Flag">Wavin'
Flag</a>&quot;
to
benefit
Haiti
in
a
movement
called
<a
href="/wiki/Young_Artists_for_Haiti?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Young
Artists
for
Haiti">Young
Artists
for
Haiti</a>.
Emily
and
Jimmy
also
performed
at
a
Neil
Young
tribute
event
along
side
their
friends
in
<a
href="/wiki/Broken_Social_Scene?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Broken
Social
Scene">Broken
Social
Scene</a>.
It
was
at
this
event
that
Emily
met
<a
href="/wiki/Lou_Reed?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lou
Reed">Lou
Reed</a>,
leading
to
many
creative
ventures
between
the
two
of
them.</p>








<p>The
track,
&quot;Black
Sheep&quot;,
was
released
on
August
10,
2010,
and
became
available
on
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/Myspace?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Myspace">Myspace</a>
page.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
is
on
the
soundtrack
for
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Scott_Pilgrim_vs._the_World?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Pilgrim
vs.
the
World">Scott
Pilgrim
vs.
the
World</a></i>.
In
the
movie
this
song
is
sung
by
<a
href="/wiki/Brie_Larson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brie
Larson">Brie
Larson</a>
who
played
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Scott_Pilgrim_characters?qsrc=3044#Supporting_characters"
title="List
of
Scott
Pilgrim
characters">Envy
Adams</a>
in
the
film.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Scott_Pilgrim?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Pilgrim">Scott
Pilgrim</a></i>
author
<a
href="/wiki/Bryan_Lee_O%27Malley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bryan
Lee
O'Malley">Bryan
Lee
O'Malley</a>
said
he
was
inspired
by
concert
photos
of
<a
href="/wiki/Emily_Haines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emily
Haines">Emily
Haines</a>
while
originally
drawing
Envy's
singing
poses.</p>








<p>The
band
toured
in
Western
USA,
before
playing
shows
in
the
Canadian
Maritimes
and
Eastern
Ontario
for
most
of
March
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Metric
also
toured
with
<a
href="/wiki/Sarah_McLachlan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sarah
McLachlan">Sarah
McLachlan</a>
for
part
of
her
2010
<a
href="/wiki/Lilith_Fair?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lilith
Fair">Lilith
Fair</a>.</p>








<p>Metric
won
two
awards
(&quot;Group
of
the
Year&quot;
and
&quot;Alternative
Album
of
the
Year&quot;
for
<i>Fantasies</i>)
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2010_Juno_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2010
Juno
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2010
Juno
Awards</a>.</p>








<p>On
June
8,
2010,
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga:_Eclipse_(soundtrack)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse
(soundtrack)"><i>Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse</i>
soundtrack</a>
was
released
featuring
Metric'
song
&quot;Eclipse
(All
Yours)&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
was
written
with
the
film's
composer,
<a
href="/wiki/Howard_Shore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Howard
Shore">Howard
Shore</a>.
An
acoustic
version
of
the
song
can
be
found
on
the
Expanded
Edition
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fantasies_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fantasies
(album)">Fantasies</a></i>.
On
July
21,
2010,
the
band
performed
the
song
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno">The
Tonight
Show
with
Jay
Leno</a></i>.</p>








<p>During
October
and
November
2010,
Metric
opened
for
<a
href="/wiki/Muse_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Muse
(band)">Muse</a>
for
seven
shows
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Resistance_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Resistance
Tour">The
Resistance
Tour</a></i>.
Later
that
year,
the
band
was
part
of
the
lineup
for
<a
href="/wiki/Voodoo_Experience?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Voodoo
Experience">Voodoo
Experience</a>
2010,
which
took
place
over
Halloween
weekend
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Orleans,
Louisiana"
class="mw-redirect">New
Orleans,
Louisiana</a>,
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
January
4,
2011,
Metric
released
an
<i>iTunes
Session
EP</i>
exclusively
on
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>,
consisting
of
8
live
tracks,
including
&quot;Hustle
Rose&quot;,
&quot;Empty&quot;
and
a
cover
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Buffalo_Springfield?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buffalo
Springfield">Buffalo
Springfield</a>
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Expecting_to_Fly_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Expecting
to
Fly
(song)">Expecting
to
Fly</a>&quot;,
and
a
30-minute
interview.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
2011,
Metric
released
a
collection
of
remixes
from
<i>Fantasies</i>
entitled
<i>Fantasies
Flashbacks</i>
through
a
collaboration
with
website
Indaba
Music.
The
band
released
all
the
individual
tracks
as
well
as
their
stems
so
that
the
general
public
could
remix
the
songs.
The
songs
were
then
submitted
online
to
Indaba
and
the
band
chose
the
winning
remixes
for
the
album.
An
unofficial
album
<i>Electrified
Fantasies</i>
featuring
14
remixes
of
songs
of
the
album
&quot;Fantasies&quot;
appeared
in
January
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tracks
were
selected
from
1767
remixes
that
arose
from
the
official
remix
contest
and
are
licensed
under
a
<a
href="/wiki/Creative_Commons?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Creative
Commons">Creative
Commons</a>
license.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Synthetica_and_Cosmopolis_.282012.E2.80.93present.29"><i>Synthetica</i>
and
<i>Cosmopolis</i>
(2012–present)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Metric_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Synthetica
and
Cosmopolis
(2012–present)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
articles:









<a
href="/wiki/Synthetica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthetica">Synthetica</a>
and









<a
href="/wiki/Cosmopolis_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cosmopolis
(film)">Cosmopolis
(film)</a>







</div>








<p>In
October
2011,
Haines
announced
that
the
band
was
nearing
completion
of
the
band's
fifth
studio
album.
The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Synthetica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthetica">Synthetica</a></i>
was
released
on
June
12,
2012
on
the
band's
own
label,
Metric
Music
International,
and
received
generally
positive
reviews.
<i>Synthetica</i>
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Gavin_Brown_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gavin
Brown
(musician)">Gavin
Brown</a>,
John
O'Mahony,
Liam
O'Neil,
James
Shaw,
and
it
was
recorded
at
Giant
Studios
(Metric's
own
studio)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Electric_Lady_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electric
Lady
Studios">Electric
Lady
Studios</a>.
The
album
also
included
a
collaboration
with
<a
href="/wiki/Lou_Reed?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lou
Reed">Lou
Reed</a>,
who
sang
with
Haines
on
&quot;Wanderlust&quot;.
For
iTunes
pre-orders,
they
included
five
instrumental
bonus
tracks,
that
were
the
basis
of
five
songs
from
the
album.
A
deluxe
version,
with
five
additional
acoustic
tracks,
was
released
on
November
20,
2012.</p>








<p>In
a
letter
posted
on
the
band's
website,
Haines
said
&quot;<i>Synthetica</i>
is
about
staying
home
and
wanting
to
crawl
out
of
your
skin
from
the
lack
of
external
stimulation...
about
forcing
yourself
to
confront
what
you
see
in
the
mirror
when
you
finally
stand
still
long
enough
to
catch
a
reflection...
about
being
able
to
identify
the
original
in
a
long
line
of
reproductions.
It's
about
what
is
real
vs
what
is
artificial&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=Metric_live_at_Coachella_2013.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:Metric
live
at
Coachella
2013.jpg">File:Metric
live
at
Coachella
2013.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










Metric
live
at

2013









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
album's
first
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Youth_Without_Youth_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Youth
Without
Youth
(song)">Youth
Without
Youth</a>&quot;
was
released
to
the
internet
on
April
30,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
followed
by
a
sneak
preview
of
&quot;Speed
the
Collapse&quot;,
which
was
released
to
the
internet
on
May
23,
2012.</p>








<p>On
May
29,
2012,
the
band
started
a
<a
href="/wiki/Hide_and_seek?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hide
and
seek"
class="mw-redirect">hide
and
seek</a>
hunt
for
fans
to
access
an
early
stream
of
<i>Synthetica</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
secretive
stream
became
available
on
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/SoundCloud?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="SoundCloud">SoundCloud</a>
page.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
A
few
days
later
the
stream
became
publicly
available.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
late
2011
it
was
announced
that
the
band
would
be
contributing
to
the
soundtrack
of
<a
href="/wiki/David_Cronenberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Cronenberg">David
Cronenberg</a>'s
2012
drama
film
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cosmopolis_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cosmopolis
(film)">Cosmopolis</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Songs
were
co-written
by
the
band
with
film
composer
<a
href="/wiki/Howard_Shore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Howard
Shore">Howard
Shore</a>
as
well
as
an
appearance
by
<a
href="/wiki/K%27naan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="K'naan">K'naan</a>
on
one
track.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
was
the
second
time
that
the
band
collaborated
with
Shore
after
their
previous
work
on
the
<i>Twilight
Saga:
Eclipse</i>
soundtrack.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
soundtrack
was
released
on
June
5,
2012
in
Canada
and
on
July
10,
2012
in
the
United
States.</p>








<p>On
August
21,
2012,
the
first
episode
of
a
<a
href="/wiki/Documentary?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Documentary"
class="mw-redirect">documentary</a>
about
the
making
of
<i>Synthetica</i>
was
released
on
the
band's
<a
href="/wiki/YouTube?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="YouTube">YouTube</a>
channel.
The
documentary
commences
during
the
initial
stages
at
the
band's
home
studio
in
Toronto,
Canada,
and
the
camera
is
also
present
at
the
recording
sessions
that
occurred
in
New
York's
<a
href="/wiki/Electric_Lady_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electric
Lady
Studios">Electric
Lady
Studios</a>.
Haines
reveals
in
the
first
episode
that
none
of
the
band
members
are
religious
and
all
work
from
&quot;a
feeling&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
wrapped
up
a
25+
tour
dates
US
Tour
on
October
14,
2012.
They
embarked
on
their
first
arena
tour
across
Canada,
which
started
in
Victoria,
BC
on
November
9,
2012
and
ended
November
24th,
2012
at
<a
href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Centre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Air
Canada
Centre">Air
Canada
Centre</a>
in
Toronto,
ON.</p>








<p>On
November
20,
2012,
Metric
released
a
deluxe
version
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Synthetica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthetica">Synthetica</a></i>,
which
featured
acoustic
versions
of
songs
on
the
album,
as
well
as
a
cover
of
&quot;Strange
Weather&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Waits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tom
Waits">Tom
Waits</a>.
On
April
12
and
19,
2013
they
performed
at
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella
Festival</a>.</p>








<p>The
band
won
three
awards
at
<a
href="/wiki/Juno_Awards_of_2013?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juno
Awards
of
2013">2013
Juno
Awards</a>:
&quot;Alternative
Album
of
the
Year&quot;
for
<i>Synthetica</i>
and
&quot;Producer
of
the
Year&quot;
for
James
Shaw.
The
art
director/designer/photographer
Justin
Broadbent
also
won
an
award
for
&quot;Recording
Package
of
the
Year&quot;
for
<i>Synthetica</i>.
In
June
2013,
<i>Synthetica</i>
was
longlisted
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/2013_Polaris_Music_Prize?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="2013
Polaris
Music
Prize">2013
Polaris
Music
Prize</a>.</p>
